<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> of the heresiarch of the church of rome letter to joseph cottle esq <\s>
<s> my dear old friend now for your little tract heresiarch church of rome <\s>
<s> i have perused it carefully and go the whole length with you in condemnation of romanism and probably much further by reason of my having passed at least three years of life in countries where romanism was the prevailing or exclusive religion and if we are to trust the declaration by their fruits ye shall know them i have stronger reasons in the privilege i have named for passing a severe condemnation upon leading parts of their faith and courses of their practice than others who have never been eye witnesses of the evils to which i allude <\s>
<s> your little publication is well timed and will i trust have such an effect as you aimed at upon the minds of its readers <\s>
<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>

<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> governor malartie lord hector of glasgow university c letter to sir w <\s>
<s> c port louis mauritius <\s>
<s> rydal mount ambleside nov <\s>
<s> dear sir william your kind letter of the 4th of august i have just received and i thank you sincerely for this mark of your attention and for the gratification it afforded me <\s>
<s> it is pleasing to see fancy amusements giving birth to works of solid profit as under the auspices of lady gomm they are doing in your island <\s>
<s> your sonnet addressed to the unfinished monument of governor malartie is conceived with appropriate feeling and just discrimination <\s>
<s> long may the finished monument last as a tribute to departed worth and as a check and restraint upon intemperate desires for change to which the inhabitants of the island may hereafter be liable <\s>
<s> before this letter reaches you the newspapers will probably have told you that i have been recently put in nomination unknown to myself for the high office of lord rector of the university of glasgow and that there was a majority of twenty one votes in my favour in opposition to the premier lord john russell <\s>
<s> the forms of the election however allowed lord john russell to be returned through the single vote of the sub rector voting for his superior <\s>
<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>
<s> men of rank or of high station with the exception of the poet campbell who was i believe educated at this university have almost invariably been chosen for a rector of this ancient university and that another exception was made in my favour by a considerable majority affords a proof that literature independent of office does not want due estimation <\s>
<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
<s> as you do not mention your own health or that of lady gomm i infer with pleasure that the climate agrees with you both <\s>
<s> that this may continue to be so is my earnest and sincere wish in which mrs <\s>
<s> believe me dear sir william faithfully yours william wordsworth 216 148 <\s>
<s> death of dora received july 10 <\s>
<s> 1847 my dear c last night i ought to have said a quarter before one this morning it pleased god to take to himself the spirit of our beloved daughter and your truly affectionate cousin <\s>
<s> she had latterly much bodily suffering under which she supported herself by prayer and gratitude to her heavenly father for granting her to the last so many of his blessings <\s>
<s> i need not write more <\s>
<s> your aunt bears up under this affliction as becomes a christian <\s>
<s> kindest love to susan of whose sympathy we are fully assured <\s>
<s> your affectionate uncle and the more so for this affliction wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 217 pray for us <\s>
<s> of the same sorrow <\s>
<s> we bear up under our affliction as well as god enables us to do <\s>
<s> my dear friend our loss is immeasurable <\s>
<s> god bless you and yours 218 our sorrow i feel is for life but god's will be done 219 217 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> to john peace esq <\s>
<s> brigham postmark cockermouth nov <\s>
<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>

<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>
<s> men of rank or of high station with the exception of the poet campbell who was i believe educated at this university have almost invariably been chosen for a rector of this ancient university and that another exception was made in my favour by a considerable majority affords a proof that literature independent of office does not want due estimation <\s>
<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
<s> as you do not mention your own health or that of lady gomm i infer with pleasure that the climate agrees with you both <\s>
<s> that this may continue to be so is my earnest and sincere wish in which mrs <\s>
<s> believe me dear sir william faithfully yours william wordsworth 216 148 <\s>

<s> she had latterly much bodily suffering under which she supported herself by prayer and gratitude to her heavenly father for granting her to the last so many of his blessings <\s>
<s> i need not write more <\s>
<s> your aunt bears up under this affliction as becomes a christian <\s>

<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> of the heresiarch of the church of rome letter to joseph cottle esq <\s>
<s> my dear old friend now for your little tract heresiarch church of rome <\s>
<s> i have perused it carefully and go the whole length with you in condemnation of romanism and probably much further by reason of my having passed at least three years of life in countries where romanism was the prevailing or exclusive religion and if we are to trust the declaration by their fruits ye shall know them i have stronger reasons in the privilege i have named for passing a severe condemnation upon leading parts of their faith and courses of their practice than others who have never been eye witnesses of the evils to which i allude <\s>
<s> your little publication is well timed and will i trust have such an effect as you aimed at upon the minds of its readers <\s>
<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> governor malartie lord hector of glasgow university c letter to sir w <\s>
<s> c port louis mauritius <\s>
<s> rydal mount ambleside nov <\s>
<s> dear sir william your kind letter of the 4th of august i have just received and i thank you sincerely for this mark of your attention and for the gratification it afforded me <\s>
<s> it is pleasing to see fancy amusements giving birth to works of solid profit as under the auspices of lady gomm they are doing in your island <\s>
<s> your sonnet addressed to the unfinished monument of governor malartie is conceived with appropriate feeling and just discrimination <\s>
<s> long may the finished monument last as a tribute to departed worth and as a check and restraint upon intemperate desires for change to which the inhabitants of the island may hereafter be liable <\s>
<s> before this letter reaches you the newspapers will probably have told you that i have been recently put in nomination unknown to myself for the high office of lord rector of the university of glasgow and that there was a majority of twenty one votes in my favour in opposition to the premier lord john russell <\s>
<s> the forms of the election however allowed lord john russell to be returned through the single vote of the sub rector voting for his superior <\s>
<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>

<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>

<s> your little publication is well timed and will i trust have such an effect as you aimed at upon the minds of its readers <\s>
<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> governor malartie lord hector of glasgow university c letter to sir w <\s>
<s> c port louis mauritius <\s>
<s> rydal mount ambleside nov <\s>
<s> dear sir william your kind letter of the 4th of august i have just received and i thank you sincerely for this mark of your attention and for the gratification it afforded me <\s>
<s> it is pleasing to see fancy amusements giving birth to works of solid profit as under the auspices of lady gomm they are doing in your island <\s>
<s> your sonnet addressed to the unfinished monument of governor malartie is conceived with appropriate feeling and just discrimination <\s>
<s> long may the finished monument last as a tribute to departed worth and as a check and restraint upon intemperate desires for change to which the inhabitants of the island may hereafter be liable <\s>
<s> before this letter reaches you the newspapers will probably have told you that i have been recently put in nomination unknown to myself for the high office of lord rector of the university of glasgow and that there was a majority of twenty one votes in my favour in opposition to the premier lord john russell <\s>
<s> the forms of the election however allowed lord john russell to be returned through the single vote of the sub rector voting for his superior <\s>
<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>
<s> men of rank or of high station with the exception of the poet campbell who was i believe educated at this university have almost invariably been chosen for a rector of this ancient university and that another exception was made in my favour by a considerable majority affords a proof that literature independent of office does not want due estimation <\s>
<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
<s> as you do not mention your own health or that of lady gomm i infer with pleasure that the climate agrees with you both <\s>
<s> that this may continue to be so is my earnest and sincere wish in which mrs <\s>
<s> believe me dear sir william faithfully yours william wordsworth 216 148 <\s>
<s> death of dora received july 10 <\s>
<s> 1847 my dear c last night i ought to have said a quarter before one this morning it pleased god to take to himself the spirit of our beloved daughter and your truly affectionate cousin <\s>
<s> she had latterly much bodily suffering under which she supported herself by prayer and gratitude to her heavenly father for granting her to the last so many of his blessings <\s>
<s> i need not write more <\s>
<s> your aunt bears up under this affliction as becomes a christian <\s>
<s> kindest love to susan of whose sympathy we are fully assured <\s>
<s> your affectionate uncle and the more so for this affliction wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 217 pray for us <\s>
<s> of the same sorrow <\s>
<s> we bear up under our affliction as well as god enables us to do <\s>
<s> my dear friend our loss is immeasurable <\s>
<s> god bless you and yours 218 our sorrow i feel is for life but god's will be done 219 217 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> to john peace esq <\s>
<s> brigham postmark cockermouth nov <\s>
<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>

<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>
<s> men of rank or of high station with the exception of the poet campbell who was i believe educated at this university have almost invariably been chosen for a rector of this ancient university and that another exception was made in my favour by a considerable majority affords a proof that literature independent of office does not want due estimation <\s>
<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
<s> as you do not mention your own health or that of lady gomm i infer with pleasure that the climate agrees with you both <\s>
<s> that this may continue to be so is my earnest and sincere wish in which mrs <\s>
<s> believe me dear sir william faithfully yours william wordsworth 216 148 <\s>

<s> she had latterly much bodily suffering under which she supported herself by prayer and gratitude to her heavenly father for granting her to the last so many of his blessings <\s>
<s> i need not write more <\s>
<s> your aunt bears up under this affliction as becomes a christian <\s>

<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> of the heresiarch of the church of rome letter to joseph cottle esq <\s>
<s> my dear old friend now for your little tract heresiarch church of rome <\s>
<s> i have perused it carefully and go the whole length with you in condemnation of romanism and probably much further by reason of my having passed at least three years of life in countries where romanism was the prevailing or exclusive religion and if we are to trust the declaration by their fruits ye shall know them i have stronger reasons in the privilege i have named for passing a severe condemnation upon leading parts of their faith and courses of their practice than others who have never been eye witnesses of the evils to which i allude <\s>
<s> your little publication is well timed and will i trust have such an effect as you aimed at upon the minds of its readers <\s>
<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> governor malartie lord hector of glasgow university c letter to sir w <\s>
<s> c port louis mauritius <\s>
<s> rydal mount ambleside nov <\s>
<s> dear sir william your kind letter of the 4th of august i have just received and i thank you sincerely for this mark of your attention and for the gratification it afforded me <\s>
<s> it is pleasing to see fancy amusements giving birth to works of solid profit as under the auspices of lady gomm they are doing in your island <\s>
<s> your sonnet addressed to the unfinished monument of governor malartie is conceived with appropriate feeling and just discrimination <\s>
<s> long may the finished monument last as a tribute to departed worth and as a check and restraint upon intemperate desires for change to which the inhabitants of the island may hereafter be liable <\s>
<s> before this letter reaches you the newspapers will probably have told you that i have been recently put in nomination unknown to myself for the high office of lord rector of the university of glasgow and that there was a majority of twenty one votes in my favour in opposition to the premier lord john russell <\s>
<s> the forms of the election however allowed lord john russell to be returned through the single vote of the sub rector voting for his superior <\s>
<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>

<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>

<s> your little publication is well timed and will i trust have such an effect as you aimed at upon the minds of its readers <\s>
<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> governor malartie lord hector of glasgow university c letter to sir w <\s>
<s> c port louis mauritius <\s>
<s> rydal mount ambleside nov <\s>
<s> dear sir william your kind letter of the 4th of august i have just received and i thank you sincerely for this mark of your attention and for the gratification it afforded me <\s>
<s> it is pleasing to see fancy amusements giving birth to works of solid profit as under the auspices of lady gomm they are doing in your island <\s>
<s> your sonnet addressed to the unfinished monument of governor malartie is conceived with appropriate feeling and just discrimination <\s>
<s> long may the finished monument last as a tribute to departed worth and as a check and restraint upon intemperate desires for change to which the inhabitants of the island may hereafter be liable <\s>
<s> before this letter reaches you the newspapers will probably have told you that i have been recently put in nomination unknown to myself for the high office of lord rector of the university of glasgow and that there was a majority of twenty one votes in my favour in opposition to the premier lord john russell <\s>
<s> the forms of the election however allowed lord john russell to be returned through the single vote of the sub rector voting for his superior <\s>
<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>
<s> men of rank or of high station with the exception of the poet campbell who was i believe educated at this university have almost invariably been chosen for a rector of this ancient university and that another exception was made in my favour by a considerable majority affords a proof that literature independent of office does not want due estimation <\s>
<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
<s> as you do not mention your own health or that of lady gomm i infer with pleasure that the climate agrees with you both <\s>
<s> that this may continue to be so is my earnest and sincere wish in which mrs <\s>
<s> believe me dear sir william faithfully yours william wordsworth 216 148 <\s>
<s> death of dora received july 10 <\s>
<s> 1847 my dear c last night i ought to have said a quarter before one this morning it pleased god to take to himself the spirit of our beloved daughter and your truly affectionate cousin <\s>
<s> she had latterly much bodily suffering under which she supported herself by prayer and gratitude to her heavenly father for granting her to the last so many of his blessings <\s>
<s> i need not write more <\s>
<s> your aunt bears up under this affliction as becomes a christian <\s>
<s> kindest love to susan of whose sympathy we are fully assured <\s>
<s> your affectionate uncle and the more so for this affliction wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 217 pray for us <\s>
<s> of the same sorrow <\s>
<s> we bear up under our affliction as well as god enables us to do <\s>
<s> my dear friend our loss is immeasurable <\s>
<s> god bless you and yours 218 our sorrow i feel is for life but god's will be done 219 217 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> to john peace esq <\s>
<s> brigham postmark cockermouth nov <\s>
<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>

<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>
<s> men of rank or of high station with the exception of the poet campbell who was i believe educated at this university have almost invariably been chosen for a rector of this ancient university and that another exception was made in my favour by a considerable majority affords a proof that literature independent of office does not want due estimation <\s>
<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
<s> as you do not mention your own health or that of lady gomm i infer with pleasure that the climate agrees with you both <\s>
<s> that this may continue to be so is my earnest and sincere wish in which mrs <\s>
<s> believe me dear sir william faithfully yours william wordsworth 216 148 <\s>

<s> she had latterly much bodily suffering under which she supported herself by prayer and gratitude to her heavenly father for granting her to the last so many of his blessings <\s>
<s> i need not write more <\s>
<s> your aunt bears up under this affliction as becomes a christian <\s>

<s> my dear friend mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth has deputed to me the acceptable office of answering your friendly letter which has followed us to brigham upon the banks of the river derwent near cockermouth the birthplace of four brothers and their sister <\s>
<s> of these four i the second am now the only one left <\s>
<s> am i wrong in supposing that you have been here <\s>
<s> in which i feel interested on mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's account who reckons that portrait much the best both as to likeness and execution of all that have been made of me and she is an excellent judge <\s>
<s> in adverting to this subject i of course presume that you would have no objection to the picture being copied if the artist were inclined to do it <\s>
<s> my paper admonishes me that i must conclude <\s>
<s> pray let me know in your next how mrs <\s>
<s> reed and your family are in health and present my good wishes to her <\s>
<s> ever your faithful and much obliged friend wm <\s>
<s> of the college of maynooth c letter to a nephew <\s>
<s> rydal mount june 30 <\s>
<s> my dear c i ought to have acknowledged my debt to you long ago but the inflammation in one of my eyes which seized me on my first arrival in london kept its ground for a long time <\s>
<s> i had your two first pamphlets read to me and immediately put them into circulation among my friends in this neighbourhood but wishing to read them myself i did not like to write to you till i had done so as there were one or two passages on which i wished to make a remark <\s>
<s> as to your arguments they are unanswerable and the three tracts do you the greatest possible credit but the torrent cannot be stemmed unless we can construct a body i will not call it a party upon a new and true principle of action as you have set forth <\s>
<s> certain questions are forced by the present conduct of government upon the mind of every observing and thinking person <\s>
<s> first and foremost are we to have a national english church or is the church of england to be regarded merely as a sect <\s>
<s> and is the right to the throne to be put on a new foundation <\s>
<s> is the present ministry prepared for this and all that must precede and follow it <\s>
<s> is ireland an integral and inseparable portion of the empire or not <\s>
<s> if it be i cannot listen to the argument in favour of endowing romanism upon the ground of superiority of numbers <\s>
<s> the romanists are not a majority in england and ireland taken as they ought to be together <\s>
<s> as to scotland it has its separate kirk by especial covenant <\s>
<s> are the ministers prepared to alter fundamentally the basis of the union between england and ireland and to construct a new one <\s>
<s> if they be let them tell us so at once <\s>
<s> in short they are involving themselves and the nation in difficulties from which there is no escape for them at least none <\s>
<s> what i have seen of your letter to lord john m i like as well as your two former tracts and i shall read it carefully at my first leisure moment 212 212 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> of the heresiarch of the church of rome letter to joseph cottle esq <\s>
<s> my dear old friend now for your little tract heresiarch church of rome <\s>
<s> i have perused it carefully and go the whole length with you in condemnation of romanism and probably much further by reason of my having passed at least three years of life in countries where romanism was the prevailing or exclusive religion and if we are to trust the declaration by their fruits ye shall know them i have stronger reasons in the privilege i have named for passing a severe condemnation upon leading parts of their faith and courses of their practice than others who have never been eye witnesses of the evils to which i allude <\s>
<s> your little publication is well timed and will i trust have such an effect as you aimed at upon the minds of its readers <\s>
<s> and now let me bid you affectionately good bye with assurance that i do and shall retain to the last a remembrance of your kindness and of the many pleasant and happy hours which at one of the most interesting periods of my life i passed in your neighbourhood and in your company <\s>
<s> ever most faithfully yours william wordsworth 213 213 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i hope to be able to send you an impression of an engraving from a picture of mr <\s>
<s> haydon representing me in the act of climbing helvellyn <\s>
<s> there is great merit in this work and the sight of it will show my meaning on the subject of expression <\s>
<s> this i think is attained but then i am stooping and the inclination of the head necessarily causes a foreshortening of the features below the nose which takes from the likeness accordingly so that upon the whole yours has the advantage especially under the circumstance of your never having seen the original <\s>
<s> wordsworth has been looking over your letters in vain to find the address of the person in london through whose hands any parcel for you might be sent <\s>
<s> pray take the trouble of repeating the address in your next letter and your request shall be attended to of sending you my two letters upon the offensive subject of a railway to and through our beautiful neighbourhood <\s>
<s> you will be sorry to hear that mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth and i have been and still are under great trouble and anxiety <\s>
<s> our daughter in law fell into bad health between three and four years ago <\s>
<s> she went with her husband to madeira where they remained nearly a year she was then advised to go to italy <\s>
<s> after a prolonged residence there her six children whom her husband returned to england for went at her earnest request to that country under their father's guidance there he was obliged on account of his duty as a clergyman to leave them <\s>
<s> four of the number resided with their mother at rome three of whom took a fever there of which the youngest as noble a boy of nearly five years as ever was seen died being seized with convulsions when the fever was somewhat subdued <\s>
<s> the father in a distracted state of mind is just gone back to italy and we are most anxious to hear the result <\s>
<s> my only surviving brother also the late master of trinity college cambridge and an inestimable person is in an alarming state of health and the only child of my eldest brother long since deceased is now languishing under mortal illness at ambleside <\s>
<s> he was educated to the medical profession and caught his illness while on duty in the mediterranean <\s>
<s> he is a truly amiable and excellent young man and will be universally regretted <\s>
<s> these sad occurrences with others of like kind have thrown my mind into a state of feeling which the other day vented itself in the two sonnets which mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth will transcribe as the best acknowledgment she can make for mrs <\s>
<s> reed's and your kindness <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> wordsworth 214 214 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> bishop white mormonites c letter to professor reed <\s>
<s> reed i was much shocked to find that my last had been despatched without acknowledgment for your kindness in sending me the admirable engraving of bishop white which i was delighted on many accounts to receive <\s>
<s> this omission was owing to the distressed state of mind in which i wrote and which i throw myself on your goodness to excuse <\s>
<s> i ought to have written again by next post but we really have been and still are in such trouble from various causes that i could not take up the pen and now must beg you to accept this statement as the only excuse which i can offer <\s>
<s> we have had such accounts from my daughter in law at rome that her mother and brother are just gone thither to support her her mother being seventy years of age <\s>
<s> do you know anything of a wretched set of religionists in your country superstitionists i ought to say called mormonites or latter day saints <\s>
<s> would you believe it <\s>
<s> a niece of mrs <\s>
<s> wordsworth's has just embarked we believe at liverpool with a set of the deluded followers of that wretch in an attempt to join their society <\s>
<s> her name is a young woman of good abilities and well educated but early in life she took from her mother and her connections a methodistical turn and has gone on in a course of what she supposes to be piety till she has come to this miserable close <\s>
<s> if you should by chance hear anything about her pray let us know <\s>
<s> the report of my brother's decease which we look for every day has not yet reached us <\s>
<s> my nephew is still lingering on from day to day <\s>
<s> ever faithfully and affectionately yours wm <\s>
<s> the print of bishop white is noble everything indeed that could be wished 215 215 memoirs ii <\s>
<s> governor malartie lord hector of glasgow university c letter to sir w <\s>
<s> c port louis mauritius <\s>
<s> rydal mount ambleside nov <\s>
<s> dear sir william your kind letter of the 4th of august i have just received and i thank you sincerely for this mark of your attention and for the gratification it afforded me <\s>
<s> it is pleasing to see fancy amusements giving birth to works of solid profit as under the auspices of lady gomm they are doing in your island <\s>
<s> your sonnet addressed to the unfinished monument of governor malartie is conceived with appropriate feeling and just discrimination <\s>
<s> long may the finished monument last as a tribute to departed worth and as a check and restraint upon intemperate desires for change to which the inhabitants of the island may hereafter be liable <\s>
<s> before this letter reaches you the newspapers will probably have told you that i have been recently put in nomination unknown to myself for the high office of lord rector of the university of glasgow and that there was a majority of twenty one votes in my favour in opposition to the premier lord john russell <\s>
<s> the forms of the election however allowed lord john russell to be returned through the single vote of the sub rector voting for his superior <\s>
<s> to say the truth i am glad of this result being too advanced in life to undertake with comfort any considerable public duty and it might have seemed ungracious to decline the office <\s>

<s> i should not have dwelt so long upon this subject had anything personal to myself occurred in which you could have taken interest <\s>
